What is Nivaro?

Nivaro is a headless CMS that provides a metadata registry on top of an existing MSSQL database, a clean RBAC permissions model, a React admin UI, and a plugin system for custom business logic extensions.

Nivaro includes a full schema editor — collections, fields, relations, and computed fields are configured through the admin UI at /data-model and stored in the nivaro_-prefixed metadata registry. The registry drives the permission-aware REST API, GraphQL schema, and admin interface automatically.

FeatureImplementation
Collections/Fields UInivaro_collections + nivaro_fields metadata registry
Roles / PermissionsRBAC via nivaro_roles + nivaro_policies
Auth (OIDC)openid-client with Microsoft OIDC (PKCE flow)
ExtensionsPlugin loader at api/extensions/
Flows / AutomationInngest + in-process flow executor
WebSockets / Real-timeSocket.io + Redis pub/sub adapter
File Managementmulter + local storage + nivaro_files
Activity Lognivaro_activity + nivaro_revisions
Mailnodemailer + LiquidJS templates (planned)
Admin UIReact 19 + Vite + shadcn/ui

Architecture

Nivaro is a pnpm monorepo with two packages: api (Fastify, port 3055) and admin (React + Vite, port 3056 in dev). In production the admin is a static bundle served by a web server or CDN; in dev, Vite proxies /api requests to the Fastify process.

LayerTechnology
API FrameworkFastify v5 — TypeScript-first plugin ecosystem
DatabaseKnex + MSSQL (tedious driver) — nivaro_ prefix tables alongside existing data
Sessions / CacheRedis (ioredis) — sessions stored as sess:<id> keys
Authopenid-client PKCE flow — Microsoft OIDC
Job QueueInngest — event-driven background jobs and flows
WebSocketsSocket.io + @socket.io/redis-adapter
Admin UIReact 19 + Vite 6 + shadcn/ui + Tanstack Query v5
Linter / FormatterBiome v2 — replaces ESLint + Prettier
 
nivaro/
├── api/src/
│   ├── index.ts          # Entry — migrations, server start
│   ├── server.ts         # Fastify instance + plugin registration
│   ├── config.ts         # Zod-validated env (loaded from .env)
│   ├── auth/             # OIDC + session helpers
│   ├── db/               # Knex instance + migrations
│   ├── extensions/       # Extension loader
│   ├── middleware/        # authenticate.ts (req.user, req.isAdmin)
│   ├── plugins/          # inngest, redis, cron, socketio
│   ├── routes/           # REST endpoints
│   └── services/         # Business logic (permissions, items, etc.)
└── admin/src/
    ├── App.tsx           # Router + AuthProvider
    ├── layouts/          # AppLayout (sidebar shell)
    ├── pages/            # One file per route
    └── lib/              # api.ts, auth.tsx, utils.ts

Prerequisites

Before running Nivaro locally you need the following installed:

  • Node.js 20+ — Nivaro uses ES modules and requires a current LTS release
  • pnpm 11 — install with npm i -g pnpm@11
  • Redis — required for sessions and the Socket.io adapter. Dev default port is 6679 to avoid conflicts with other local Redis instances
  • MSSQL database — SQL Server 2019+, Azure SQL, or LocalDB. Nivaro auto-creates all nivaro_* system tables via migrations on first startup
  • Microsoft OIDC app registration — required for SSO login. Can be skipped locally if you use static tokens instead

Clone & install

git clone https://github.com/nodeworks/nivaro.git
cd nivaro
pnpm install
cp .env.example .env

Edit .env with your database connection details, Redis URL, OIDC credentials, and session secret. See the Environment Variables section for the full reference.

Run in dev mode

Start all services with a single command:

pnpm dev

This runs concurrently: Redis (port 6679), Inngest dev server, Fastify API (port 3055, tsx watch), and the Vite admin dev server (port 3056, proxies /api to 3055). Run services individually with:

pnpm dev:api       # Fastify API only
pnpm dev:admin     # Admin UI only
pnpm dev:redis     # Redis only
pnpm dev:inngest   # Inngest dev server only
Do NOT use --env-file when invoking tsx — it breaks watch mode. Environment variables are loaded via dotenv inside api/src/config.ts.

On first startup the API runs all pending migrations before opening the HTTP server. Look for:

Migrations ran: 001_initial, 002_roles, ...
Server listening on http://0.0.0.0:3055

First steps

  1. Open the admin UI at http://localhost:3056
  2. Log in via Microsoft OIDC, or set a static token on your user and authenticate with Bearer auth
  3. Navigate to Settings and confirm DB and Redis show healthy status
  4. Go to Collections and register your first business table
  5. Go to Roles, create a role, and add a policy granting read access to your collection
  6. Go to Users and assign the role to your account

Once a collection is registered and you have an active read policy, the collection browser at Collections will display its rows and let you open records in the item editor.

Dashboard

The dashboard is the first screen after login. It shows live system health, key counts, and recent activity.

System health bar

The colored indicator at the top right of the info panel reflects the state of both the database and Redis connections. It refreshes every 30 seconds automatically. If either service is unreachable the indicator turns amber and shows "System degraded."

Stats cards

Counts for Collections, Users, Active Flows, and Extensions. These are live queries — no manual refresh needed.

Recent activity

The last 10 entries from the nivaro_activity audit log, shown in reverse chronological order. Click any entry to see the related record.

Collections

The Collections page lists every table registered in the nivaro_collections metadata registry. Clicking a collection opens a paginated data browser for that table.

Browsing data

The collection browser displays up to 25 rows per page by default. Use the search box at the top to filter rows across all string and text fields. Clicking a row opens the item editor.

Field metadata

Field display names, types, and visibility are controlled by entries in nivaro_fields. Hidden fields are not shown in the UI. Read-only fields are displayed but not editable. These are registered by an administrator — the UI has no schema editor.

Only tables registered in nivaro_collections are browsable. Business tables must be registered by an administrator using the collections API or a seed script.

Column Presets

The collection browser lets you choose which columns to display and in what order. Your selection is saved as a preset so it persists across sessions. Admins can also set a system default that applies to all users who have not chosen their own preset.

Opening the column picker

Click the Columns button in the top-right toolbar of any collection browser. A popover opens with:

  • Visible columns — drag handles let you reorder. Click the × to hide a column.
  • Add column — a searchable list of all available fields not already visible.
  • Your presets — saved column configurations. Click one to activate it. The active preset name is shown as a badge on the Columns button.
  • Save as preset — saves the current column/order selection under a name of your choice.
  • Set as system default (admin only) — saves the current selection as the default for all users who have not set their own preset.

Preset resolution order

When loading a collection browser, columns are resolved in this priority:

  • Your active preset (if you have activated one for this collection).
  • The system default (if an admin has set one for this collection).
  • The first 7 fields from the collection's field list (built-in fallback).

Deleting or renaming a preset

In the column picker popover, hover over a saved preset and click the trash icon to delete it. To rename, delete and re-save with the new name.

Presets are stored per collection per user in nivaro_collection_presets. The system default has user_id = NULL. Each user can have multiple named presets but only one active at a time (tracked server-side).

Users & Roles

Users

The Users page lists all Nivaro users. Users are created automatically on first Microsoft OIDC login, or manually by an administrator.

  • **Status** — active users can log in; suspended users are blocked at the authenticate middleware.
  • **Role** — each user has one role. Role assignment controls what collections and actions are permitted.
  • **Admin access** — if the assigned role has admin_access: true, all permission checks are bypassed.

Roles & Permissions

Roles are defined in nivaro_roles. Each role has zero or more policies (in nivaro_policies) that grant access.

Policy fieldDescription
collectionTable name the policy applies to, e.g. articles
actionOne of: read, create, update, delete
fieldsOptional JSON array of allowed field names. Null = all fields.

Policies are additive — a user with two policies granting read on different field sets gets the union of those fields.

Deleting a role that has users assigned to it is blocked. Reassign users to another role first.

My Profile

The Profile page lets any authenticated user manage their own account. Access it by clicking your name or avatar in the sidebar footer.

What you can change

  • First name / Last name — editable. Changes take effect immediately in the sidebar and across the UI.
  • Email — read-only. Managed via Microsoft OIDC; cannot be changed here.

Read-only account details

Role name, account status, User ID, member since date, and last access time are displayed but not editable by a regular user. Admins can change role and status via the Users page.

API token management

The API Token section lets you manage your static token for programmatic API access:

  • Generate — creates a new token. The value is shown once — copy it immediately.
  • Reveal / Hide — toggles visibility of the token value.
  • Copy — copies the token to the clipboard (only available while revealed).
  • Regenerate — replaces the existing token with a new one. The old token stops working immediately.
  • Revoke — deletes the token entirely. Bearer-token API access is disabled until a new token is generated.

Revision history

A History button in the page header opens the revision panel showing every change made to your user record (name changes, role assignments, status changes).

Tokens are shown only on generation. If you close the page without copying, the token value cannot be retrieved — regenerate to get a new one.

Flows

Flows are automated workflows. Each flow has a trigger (how it starts) and a sequence of operations (what it does).

Triggers

TriggerDescription
manualStarted by clicking "Run Flow" in the UI or calling POST /api/flows/:id/trigger
scheduleRuns on a cron schedule. Specify a cron expression in Trigger Options.
eventTriggered by an Inngest event name (planned).
webhookTriggered by an incoming HTTP request (planned).

Operations

Operations run in order of their position (top to bottom, left to right). Output from each operation is passed to the next as the flow's data payload.

TypeStatusDescription
log✅ LiveWrites a structured line to the API server log (pino). Configure message and level in options.
webhook✅ LiveHTTP fetch to an external URL. Configure url and method in options.
condition⚙️ StubBranch on a condition expression (not yet implemented — resolves forward).
exec-script⚙️ StubRun arbitrary Node.js code (not yet implemented).
mail⚙️ StubSend email via nodemailer (not yet implemented).
notification⚙️ StubCreate an in-app notification (not yet implemented).

Configuring a log operation

Click the pencil icon on any operation row to open the options editor. For a log operation:

  • **Message** — the text written to the server log. Defaults to the operation name if left blank.
  • **Level** — info, warn, error, or debug. Log output appears in the API process stdout (visible in pnpm dev:api).

Status

Only active flows execute. Toggling a flow to inactive immediately unregisters its cron job. Scheduled flows are re-registered automatically when the API restarts.

Files

The file manager lets you upload, browse, and delete files. Uploaded files are stored on local disk and metadata is tracked in nivaro_files.

EndpointDescription
POST /api/filesUpload a file (multipart/form-data). Returns nivaro_files metadata.
GET /api/files/:id/contentServe the file with correct Content-Type.
DELETE /api/files/:idDelete file from disk and remove metadata.

Extensions

Extensions are Node.js plugins that extend Nivaro's behavior — custom routes, hooks, scheduled jobs, and Inngest functions. The Extensions page shows all discovered plugins and their status.

StatusMeaning
loadedExtension is registered and active.
errorExtension was found but threw an error during registration.
missingEntry exists in config but the folder no longer exists on disk.

Use the toggle switch to enable or disable an extension without removing it. Disabled extensions have their hooks skipped and cron jobs paused. The enabled state persists across restarts via api/extensions/.config.json.

Click **Scan for new** to pick up any extensions added to api/extensions/ since the server started, without restarting.

Missing extensions (folder deleted but config entry remains) can be removed by clicking the trash icon on the amber card.

Settings

App-wide settings stored in the nivaro_settings singleton row (always id = 1). All fields are configurable via **Settings** in the admin sidebar. Changes take effect immediately unless noted.

Project

FieldDescription
project_nameName shown in the browser tab and sidebar logo area.
project_descriptionShort subtitle shown under the logo when the sidebar is expanded.
project_urlPublic URL of the application (used in emails, notifications, etc.).
project_colorAccent hex color used in the sidebar and UI highlights.
default_languageLocale string, e.g. en-US.

Microsoft

FieldDescription
teams_webhook_urlIncoming webhook URL — in-app notifications are also posted here.
ad_group_role_mapJSON array of { ad_group_id, role_id } mappings. First match wins on OIDC login.

AI Features

FieldDefaultDescription
anthropic_api_key—Anthropic API key. Masked on GET. Falls back to ANTHROPIC_API_KEY env var.
ai_modelclaude-haiku-4-5-20251001Model used for all AI generate and summarize requests.
ai_max_tokens_generate500Token budget for /ai/generate.
ai_max_tokens_summarize200Token budget for /ai/summarize.

Presence Tracking

FieldDefaultDescription
presence_session_ttl20Redis TTL (seconds) for a session after the last ping. Must exceed the ping interval.
presence_sweep_interval8000How often (ms) the server pushes the current session list to the admin presence page.
presence_ping_interval10000How often (ms) the embedded tracker script pings the server. Takes effect on next script load.

SLA

FieldDefaultDescription
sla_business_day_start9Start of the business day (24h hour, inclusive) for business-hours SLA calculations.
sla_business_day_end17End of the business day (24h hour, exclusive) for business-hours SLA calculations.
sla_business_days1,2,3,4,5Comma-separated day numbers (0=Sun … 6=Sat) treated as working days.

Content

FieldDefaultDescription
file_max_size_mb50Max file upload size in MB. Read at server startup — requires restart after change.
collection_page_size25Default rows per page in the collection browser.
activity_retention_daysnullDelete activity log entries older than N days. Null = keep forever. Purge runs daily.
revision_retention_countnullKeep only the most recent N revisions per record. Null = keep all. Purge runs daily.

Activity Log

Every create, update, and delete on a tracked collection is recorded in nivaro_activity. The Activity page shows a paginated, filterable audit log.

For item mutations, a nivaro_revisions row stores the full JSON snapshot and a delta of changed fields, allowing point-in-time restoration.

Activity logging middleware is planned — the tables exist and are written to by flow triggers, but automatic logging of generic item mutations has not yet been wired up.

In-App Notifications

Nivaro delivers real-time in-app notifications via Socket.io. The bell icon in the sidebar header shows an unread count badge and lists the last 10 notifications in a popover.

Real-time delivery

The admin UI connects to Socket.io on load and authenticates using the current user's static token. Incoming notification:new events immediately update the unread badge and show a toast. No page refresh needed.

Notification schema

ColumnDescription
recipientFK → nivaro_users.id — the target user.
senderFK → nivaro_users.id — who sent it (nullable).
subjectShort title shown in the bell popover and toast.
messageFull notification body (nullable).
status"inbox" (unread) or "read".
collection / itemOptional link to a specific record.
timestampWhen the notification was created.

REST endpoints

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/notificationsList last 50 notifications for the current user. ?unread=true for inbox only.
GET/api/notifications/countReturns { unread: N } — used to drive the badge.
POST/api/notifications/:id/readMark a single notification as read.
POST/api/notifications/read-allMark all inbox notifications as read.
DELETE/api/notifications/:idDelete a notification.

Emitting from server code

import { emitNotification } from '../plugins/socketio.js';

// Inside a route or hook — app.io is the Socket.io server
emitNotification(app.io, targetUserId, {
  subject: 'Project approved',
  message: 'Your request was approved by Finance.',
  collection: 'projects',
  item: projectId,
});
The Socket.io bell uses the user's static token for authentication. If a user has no static token, real-time delivery is unavailable but they can still poll the REST endpoints.

Comments & Mentions

Every item edit page includes a Comments panel. Users can post, edit, and delete comments on any record. Mentioning another user with @handle sends them an in-app notification and, if a Teams webhook is configured, a Microsoft Teams card.

Posting a comment

Type in the comment input and submit. Use @email-prefix or @first_name to mention Nivaro users — the server resolves handles on submit, so no autocomplete is required.

Mentions

When a user is mentioned they receive:

  • An in-app notification in the bell popover (real-time via Socket.io).
  • A Microsoft Teams MessageCard (requires teams_webhook_url in Settings).

Editing and deleting

Authors can edit or delete their own comments. Admins can edit or delete any comment.

Computed Fields

Fields can have a formula that is evaluated automatically. Formulas use expr-eval — a safe, sandboxed arithmetic/logical expression evaluator. No arbitrary code execution.

Compute types

TypeWhen evaluatedStored in DB?Use case
readOn every GET requestNo — virtual key added to responseDerived display values (full name, total price)
write (not stored)Before INSERT / UPDATENoTransformations that should not persist
write + storeBefore INSERT / UPDATEYes — written to the DB columnSearchable / sortable derived columns
rollupOn every GET requestNo — virtual key added to responseAggregates of related items (sum of line totals, child count)

Rollup fields

A rollup field returns an aggregate (sum / count / avg / min / max) of related items in another collection. Instead of an expression, the formula is a JSON config object describing what to aggregate. Like read-time fields, rollups are virtual — computed fresh on every read, never stored.

{
  "related_collection": "line_items",  // table to aggregate from
  "fk_field": "workflow_id",            // column on related_collection → this item's id
  "aggregate": "sum",                   // sum | count | avg | min | max
  "value_field": "amount",              // column to aggregate (ignored for count)
  "recursive": false                    // optional — see below
}

Example: on a workflow record, a rollup with related_collection: "line_items", fk_field: "workflow_id", aggregate: "sum", value_field: "amount" returns the total of all line item amounts pointing at that workflow.

Recursive (tree) rollups

Set recursive: true when related_collection is the SAME collection as the field's own collection and that collection forms a self-referential tree (the fk_field points at a parent row's id). The rollup then aggregates every descendant at any depth — children, grandchildren, and beyond — using a recursive SQL CTE (capped at 100 levels). Use this for "sum of all costs under this node" style totals across an org/category tree.

The Recursive checkbox in the UI only appears when the related collection equals the collection being edited. When the related collection differs, recursive is ignored and a plain single-level aggregate runs.

Configure rollups in Data Model → table → expand a field → Computed Formula → enable → choose Rollup (aggregate). Pick the related collection, FK field, aggregate function, and value field from the comboboxes. The value field is disabled for count.

Configuring in the UI

Go to Data Model in the sidebar → click a table → expand any field row → scroll to the Computed Formula section:

1. Check Enable to activate the formula editor. 2. Choose Read (virtual) or Write (before save). 3. Enter a formula using item.fieldName syntax. 4. For write-type, optionally check Store result in database column. 5. Click Save on the field row.

Formula syntax

The formula context provides the full record as item:

// Numeric
item.quantity * item.unit_price
item.discount > 0 ? item.amount * (1 - item.discount / 100) : item.amount

// String — use || for concatenation (+ is numeric only)
item.first_name || " " || item.last_name

// String helpers
concat(item.first_name, " ", item.last_name)   // nulls skipped
join(", ", item.city, item.state, item.zip)     // empty values skipped
upper(item.code)
lower(item.email)
trim(item.notes)
substr(item.sku, 0, 3)
replace(item.slug, "-", "_")
coalesce(item.nickname, item.first_name)        // first non-null/empty wins

// Conditional
item.status == "active" ? 1 : 0
String concatenation: use || or the concat() helper — not +. The + operator is numeric; using it on strings produces NaN. The concat() and join() helpers automatically skip null/undefined values.

In the item editor

Computed fields are excluded from the editable Fields section. They appear in a separate Computed Values card (with a function icon in the header) showing the current server-evaluated value, a read-time or write-time badge, and the formula displayed beneath each value. The card is read-only — computed values cannot be manually edited.

In the collection browser

Computed columns are marked with a small violet ⊡ icon in the column header. Hovering shows the formula. Read-time values are fresh on every page load; write-time stored values reflect the last save.

Configuring via API

POST /api/collections/:collection/fields
{
  "field": "total_price",
  "computed_formula": "item.quantity * item.unit_price",
  "computed_type": "read",    // "read" | "write" | "rollup"
  "computed_store": false     // true = persist result to DB column (write-type only)
}

// Rollup — computed_formula is a JSON string config:
{
  "field": "line_total",
  "computed_type": "rollup",
  "computed_formula": "{\"related_collection\":\"line_items\",\"fk_field\":\"workflow_id\",\"aggregate\":\"sum\",\"value_field\":\"amount\"}",
  "computed_store": false
}
Write-time + stored computed fields require the target column to already exist in the database schema. Read-time fields add a virtual key to API responses without touching the schema.

GraphQL

Computed fields appear in the auto-generated GraphQL schema exactly like regular scalar fields — no special handling required. Read-time virtual fields are populated by the query resolver (which calls readItems server-side). Write-time fields reflect the stored or last-evaluated value.

query {
  articles_by_id(id: "123") {
    id
    title
    full_name        # read-time computed — evaluated fresh on every query
    total_price      # write+store computed — stored in DB, returned as-is
  }
}

SDK

Computed field values are included transparently in all item responses. No special SDK commands are needed — readItems and readItem return them alongside regular fields.

import { readItem } from '@nivaro/sdk'

const article = await nivaro.request(readItem('articles', '123'))
// article.data.full_name   → computed read-time value (evaluated server-side)
// article.data.total_price → computed write+store value

Dashboards

The Dashboards page lets you build KPI dashboards composed of metric widgets. Dashboards are personal by default; admins can mark them shared so all users see them.

Widget types

TypeDescription
countTotal row count for a collection.
sumSum of a numeric field across all rows.
avgAverage of a numeric field.
latestTable of the 10 most recently created records.
bar_chartBar chart of record creation counts over the last 30 days.
line_chartLine chart of creation counts over the last 30 days.

Creating a dashboard

Click + New Dashboard, give it a name, and optionally check Shared. Add widgets using + Add Widget in the toolbar.

Shared dashboards

Shared dashboards appear in every user's list but can only be edited by the owner or an admin.

Audit & Compliance Reports

The Reports page (admin-only) provides filtered views of the audit log with CSV export for compliance workflows.

Activity report

Filter by collection, user, action (create/update/delete), and date range. Results are paginated in the UI. Click Export CSV to download the full filtered dataset with no row limit.

Summary report

Aggregated counts for the selected date range: breakdown by action type, top collections by mutation volume, and top users by activity count.

Reports require admin access. Non-admin users cannot access this page or its API.

Workspaces

Workspaces provide logical separation within a single Nivaro instance. Collections and roles are scoped to a workspace. Users can switch workspaces without logging out.

Switching workspaces

Click the workspace name at the bottom of the sidebar to open the switcher popover. Select a workspace to switch — the page reloads with the new context applied.

Workspace isolation

Every API request includes an x-workspace header (sent automatically by the admin UI). The server uses this to scope collections and roles. If omitted, the server falls back to the user's saved preference, then the default workspace.

Workspace isolation applies to collections and roles — which collections appear in the sidebar and which roles exist for assignment. Data rows (items) are not filtered by workspace; all records in a table are visible regardless of active workspace. Full row-level isolation would require a workspace_id FK column per business table and can be added in a future migration.

Managing workspaces

Admins can create, edit, and delete workspaces via the Workspaces page in the sidebar. Each workspace needs a unique slug. The default workspace cannot be deleted.

External APIs

External APIs lets you configure connections to third-party services (Oracle EBS, MWF, MDSi, Azure, etc.) with stored authentication credentials. Configured APIs can be tested from the admin UI and called programmatically from extensions.

Admin UI — /external-apis

Navigate to External APIs in the sidebar. Each entry shows the base URL, auth type, and enabled state. Click an entry to open the editor with three tabs: config, predefined endpoints, and the live test panel.

Auth types

TypeHow it works
noneNo auth headers added.
bearerAdds Authorization: Bearer <token> to every request.
api_keyInjects a key/value pair as a header or query param (configurable).
basicAdds Authorization: Basic base64(username:password).
oauth2_ccFetches a client credentials token from token_url on each call, then injects as Bearer.

Predefined endpoint templates

Each API can store a library of named endpoint templates — method, path, default body, default query params, default headers, and an optional description. Templates appear as color-coded pills in the test panel. Clicking a pill pre-fills all fields; you can then override any value before running the test.

Manage endpoints in the Endpoints card on the API edit page. Each row is expandable inline — add, edit, and delete without leaving the page. The body field includes a Format button that pretty-prints JSON.

Test panel

The test panel supports full request composition: method selector, path, body textarea (shown for POST/PUT/PATCH), collapsible query params and request headers editors, and a response section that shows status, body, and toggleable response headers. Use the Custom pill for ad-hoc requests or select a predefined endpoint pill to start from its defaults.

Security

Secrets (token, password, client_secret, api_key value) are masked in GET responses with ••••••. Re-submitting the masked value on PATCH preserves the existing secret. Only admins can read or write API configs.

External APIs intentionally skip SSRF protection — they are admin-only and designed to reach internal corporate services (Oracle EBS, MWF, MDSi, etc.) that would otherwise be blocked. SSRF protection applies to webhooks, not external APIs.

Custom Queries

Custom queries let admins expose parameterized SQL as named REST endpoints. They appear under /custom-queries in the sidebar.

Creating a query

Go to Custom Queries → New Query. Fill in:

FieldDescription
NameHuman-readable label.
SlugURL identifier — auto-derived from the name, editable. Used as the endpoint slug.
SQLRaw SQL. Use :paramName placeholders for dynamic values.
Access"authenticated" (any logged-in user) or "admin" (admin only).
Cache TTLSeconds to cache results. 0 disables caching.
ParametersDefine name, type (string/number/boolean), default value, and required flag.

Executing

Once saved, the query is available at POST /api/custom-queries/:slug/execute with a JSON body { "params": { "region": "West" } }. Use the Test Execute panel in the editor to run it live with sample values.

SDK

import { listCustomQueries, executeCustomQuery } from '@nivaro/sdk'

const { data } = await nivaro.request(
  executeCustomQuery('active-orders-by-region', { region: 'West' })
)

Presence Tracking

Presence lets you see which external users are active on your site right now. The embedded tracker script pings the API on a configurable interval; sessions expire automatically from Redis when pings stop. The admin Presence page updates in near real-time via Socket.io.

Embedding the tracker

Serve the script from your Nivaro API and add it to any page you want to track:

<script
  src="https://your-api.example.com/api/presence.js"
  data-api-url="https://your-api.example.com"
  data-user-id="user-123"
  data-user-email="jane@example.com"
  data-user-name="Jane Smith"
></script>

All data-* attributes are optional. Alternatively, set a window.NivaroPresence config object before the script tag:

window.NivaroPresence = {
  apiUrl: 'https://your-api.example.com',
  userId: currentUser.id,
  userEmail: currentUser.email,
  userName: currentUser.name,
};

Runtime API

After the script loads, window.NivaroPresenceClient is available:

MethodDescription
ping()Send an immediate ping (called automatically on interval).
disconnect()Remove this session from Redis immediately.
setUser(id, email, name)Update the identity for the current session — use in SPAs after login.
trackView(prevDur)Manually record a page view (called automatically on navigation).
sessionIdThe current session UUID (read-only).

Timing configuration

Ping interval, server sweep interval, and session TTL are all configurable in Settings → Presence. The session TTL must be longer than the ping interval or sessions will expire between pings. Ping interval changes take effect when the script is next loaded (no server restart required).

User identity fields (userId, userEmail, userName) are client-asserted and cannot be verified for public tracker requests. Display them as "self-reported" rather than treating them as authoritative.

Frontend Analytics

The same tracker script that powers Presence also records page views into nivaro_page_views. No extra configuration is needed — page view tracking is active as soon as the script is embedded.

What is tracked

FieldDescription
pageUrlFull URL of the page viewed.
pageTitledocument.title at view time.
referrerdocument.referrer (empty on direct navigation).
deviceTypedesktop, tablet, or mobile (UA-sniffed).
duration_secondsTime spent on the page. Recorded when the user navigates away or closes the tab.
session_idPersistent session UUID stored in localStorage.
user_email / user_nameClient-asserted identity from the tracker config (self-reported).

SPA navigation

The script hooks history.pushState and the popstate event so single-page app route changes are tracked automatically. Each navigation closes the previous view (recording its duration) and opens a new one.

Analytics page

Navigate to Monitoring → Analytics. The page shows:

PanelDescription
Stat cardsTotal views, unique sessions, and unique pages for the selected period.
Views tablePaginated list of individual page views with URL, identity, device, and duration.
Top pagesBar chart of the most-visited URLs by view count for the selected period.

Period options: Today (1d), 7 Days, 30 Days.

Page view durations are written on navigation or tab close via fetch + keepalive. If the browser is force-killed the final duration may not be recorded.

Local Dev

Run Nivaro directly on your machine without Docker. Requires Node.js 20+, pnpm 11, a running Redis instance, and an MSSQL database reachable from your machine.

npm i -g pnpm@11
git clone https://github.com/nodeworks/nivaro.git
cd nivaro
pnpm install
cp .env.example .env   # then fill in DB_HOST, OIDC_*, SESSION_SECRET

pnpm dev

Starts all services concurrently — Redis, Inngest, the Fastify API (tsx watch), and the Vite admin dev server:

pnpm dev

On first run the API executes all pending migrations before opening the HTTP listener. Look for Server listening on http://0.0.0.0:3055 before opening the admin UI.

Do not pass --env-file to tsx — it bypasses dotenv and breaks watch mode. Variables are loaded inside api/src/config.ts.

Individual services

pnpm dev:api       # Fastify API only (tsx watch, port 3055)
pnpm dev:admin     # Vite admin UI only (port 3056, proxies /api → 3055)
pnpm dev:redis     # Redis only
pnpm dev:inngest   # Inngest dev server only

Ports

ServicePortNotes
Fastify API3055REST + GraphQL + Socket.io
Admin UI3056Vite dev server; /api proxied to 3055
Redis6679Non-standard port to avoid conflicts with other local instances
Inngest8288Self-hosted dev server dashboard

Dev Docker

When developing Nivaro itself, the repo includes a docker-compose.yml that builds the API and admin from source and spins up all required backing services:

pnpm dev:docker   # starts all services via Docker Compose

The release image (Dockerfile.release) bundles the compiled API and the admin SPA as static files, both served from the same Fastify process on port 3055.

Services

ServicePortDescription
redis6379Redis — sessions + Socket.io adapter
postgres5432Postgres — Inngest event/run history store
inngest8288Inngest self-hosted server (backed by Postgres + Redis)
api3055Fastify API (dev build)
admin3056React admin UI (nginx)

Your MSSQL database runs externally (on-premises or Azure SQL). The compose file does not manage it — connect via the DB_* environment variables.

COOKIE_SECURE must be false when running on plain HTTP (the Docker default). If set to true on an HTTP connection, the session cookie is silently dropped and OIDC login breaks with no visible error.

Inngest signing key

Inngest requires a real 64-character hex signing key in Docker environments. The local dev value of local is not accepted by the self-hosted Inngest container.

Use a separate env variable to avoid the local value leaking from your .env into Docker:

# In .env
INNGEST_SIGNING_KEY=local              # used by tsx dev
INNGEST_SIGNING_KEY_DOCKER=abcdef...   # 64-char hex, used by docker-compose

Generate a suitable key with:

node -e "console.log(require('crypto').randomBytes(32).toString('hex'))"

Environment Variables

All variables are loaded from a .env file at the repo root via dotenv in api/src/config.ts. A starter file is at examples/my-project/.env.example.

Database

Nivaro connects to MSSQL via the tedious driver through Knex. The database is your existing MSSQL server — Nivaro does not manage it.

VariableDefaultDescription
DB_HOST—MSSQL server hostname or IP
DB_PORT1433MSSQL port
DB_DATABASE—Database name
DB_USER—SQL login username
DB_PASSWORD—SQL login password
DB_ENCRYPTtrueEncrypt the connection (required by Azure SQL)
DB_TRUST_SERVER_CERTtrueTrust self-signed server certificate
NODE_TLS_REJECT_UNAUTHORIZED1Set to 0 for on-premises SQL Server with internal CA certs. Not needed for Azure SQL with a publicly-trusted cert.

Auth & Session

Microsoft OIDC requires an app registration in your Azure AD tenant. The redirect URI must match your PUBLIC_URL exactly.

VariableDescription
OIDC_ISSUERhttps://login.microsoftonline.com/{tenant-id}/v2.0
OIDC_CLIENT_IDAzure app registration client ID
OIDC_CLIENT_SECRETAzure app registration client secret
OIDC_REDIRECT_URIMust be {PUBLIC_URL}/api/auth/callback
SESSION_SECRETRandom string, minimum 32 characters
SESSION_TTLSession lifetime in seconds (default 86400)
COOKIE_SECUREfalse for HTTP; true only when Fastify itself receives HTTPS
COOKIE_SECURE=true on a plain HTTP connection silently drops the session cookie — the OIDC callback succeeds but the user is immediately redirected back to login with no visible error. Always use false in Docker or any HTTP environment.

URLs

VariableDescription
PUBLIC_URLAPI base URL — used for OIDC redirect and mail links. In the release image, same as ADMIN_URL.
ADMIN_URLAdmin UI URL. Same as PUBLIC_URL in the single-container release image; separate in dev (:3056).

Redis

VariableDescription
REDIS_URLRedis connection URL. Overridden to redis://redis:6379 inside Docker Compose.

Redis backs session storage (@fastify/session), the Socket.io pub/sub adapter, and Inngest event brokering. A standard Redis 6+ instance with no extra modules is sufficient.

Inngest

VariableDescription
INNGEST_EVENT_KEYlocal in dev; real key in production
INNGEST_SIGNING_KEYlocal in dev; 64-char hex in production
INNGEST_SIGNING_KEY_DOCKERDocker-only override. Holds the real 64-char hex key so the local value in .env never leaks into the container.
INNGEST_BASE_URLInngest server URL. Set to http://inngest:8288 inside Docker Compose.

Generate a signing key with openssl rand -hex 32.

Mail

Mail is a no-op when SMTP_HOST is unset or localhost. MAIL_FROM must match the authenticated SMTP account.

VariableDescription
MAIL_FROMSender address, e.g. Nivaro <no-reply@example.com>
SMTP_HOSTSMTP server hostname
SMTP_PORTSMTP port (default 587)
SMTP_SECUREfalse for STARTTLS on 587; true for TLS on 465
SMTP_USERSMTP login username
SMTP_PASSWORDSMTP login password

AI Features

VariableDescription
ANTHROPIC_API_KEYOptional. If unset, the AI routes fall back to the key stored in nivaro_settings.anthropic_api_key, configurable from Settings → AI Features. Always masked on GET.

Metadata registry

Nivaro does not own your database schema. Instead, you register existing MSSQL tables as collections by creating entries in nivaro_collections. This tells Nivaro which tables to expose through the REST API, GraphQL, and admin UI — without modifying the table DDL.

Each collection entry includes a display name, workspace scope, and optional icon and color for the admin UI sidebar. Collections are workspace-scoped: the same physical table can appear under different configurations in different workspaces.

In the admin UI, navigate to Collections to browse registered collections. The Data Model section (/data-model) provides field and relation configuration. The collection browser at /collections/:name shows a paginated data table for each registered collection.

Fields

Field metadata is stored in nivaro_fields. Fields control how each column is displayed and edited in the admin UI — the actual MSSQL column is not affected.

Field attributeDescription
typeData type hint: string, integer, boolean, datetime, json, etc.
interfaceAdmin UI widget: input, textarea, select, toggle, datetime, file, relation
hiddenWhen true the field is not shown in the item editor or collection browser
requiredEnforces client-side validation in the item editor
sortInteger controlling display order
computed_formulaJavaScript expression evaluated server-side for computed fields
computed_typeReturn type of the computed formula: string, number, or boolean
Hidden fields are excluded from API responses when the requesting user's policy does not explicitly list them. They are never shown in the admin UI item editor.

Relations

Relations are registered in nivaro_relations and describe how collections reference each other. Nivaro supports four relation types:

  • M2O (many-to-one) — a foreign key on the current collection pointing to another collection
  • O2M (one-to-many) — the reverse side of an M2O, listing related items in a sub-panel
  • M2M (many-to-many) — via a junction table; both sides are listed with an add/remove UI
  • M2A (many-to-any) — polymorphic relation pointing to any registered collection

The admin UI uses relation metadata to render relation pickers in the item editor and to traverse dotted-path field references in pipeline dimensions and computed fields.

Collections API

All collections endpoints are under /api/collections and require admin access.

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/collectionsList all collections for the current workspace
GET/api/collections/:nameGet a single collection with its fields and relations
POST/api/collectionsRegister a new collection
PATCH/api/collections/:nameUpdate collection metadata
DELETE/api/collections/:nameUnregister a collection (does not drop the table)

CRUD operations

The items API provides permission-aware CRUD for every registered collection. All endpoints are under /api/items/:collection. The requesting user must have a matching policy in nivaro_policies — if not, the server returns 403 Forbidden.

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/items/:collectionList items with filter, sort, page, limit
GET/api/items/:collection/:idGet a single item by primary key
POST/api/items/:collectionCreate a new item; writes activity + revision
PATCH/api/items/:collection/:idPartial update; captures previousData for hooks and delta revision
DELETE/api/items/:collection/:idDelete item; writes activity entry

Every mutation automatically writes to the nivaro_activity audit log and creates a full snapshot in nivaro_revisions. Updates also compute and store a delta of only the changed fields. Revisions are accessible from the item editor via the Revisions side panel.

Filtering

Pass a filter query parameter as a JSON object. Each key is a field name and the value is either a direct equality value or an operator object:

GET /api/items/articles?filter={"status":"published"}
GET /api/items/articles?filter={"views":{"_gte":100}}
GET /api/items/articles?filter={"status":"published","views":{"_gte":100}}

Available operators: _eq, _neq, _lt, _lte, _gt, _gte, _in, _nin, _null, _nnull, _contains, _starts_with, _ends_with. Logical operators _and and _or accept arrays of condition objects.

Pagination

Items are paginated using page and limit query parameters:

GET /api/items/articles?page=2&limit=25&sort=-created_at

The response envelope includes data (array of items), total (total matching row count), page, and limit. The sort parameter accepts comma-separated field names; prefix with - for descending order.

MSSQL requires an ORDER BY clause when using OFFSET/FETCH. If no sort is specified, Nivaro automatically appends ORDER BY (SELECT NULL) to satisfy MSSQL requirements.

Hooks

The hook system fires synchronously before and after every item mutation. Extensions register hooks via the hooks context object. Built-in hooks handle activity logging, revision writing, field watches, SLA checks, and alert evaluation.

The HookContext passed to every hook includes:

  • collection — the table name
  • action — create, update, or delete
  • payload — the data being written (before hooks can modify this)
  • item — the item after the operation (after hooks only)
  • previousData — a snapshot of the row before the update or delete (captured before the write, so no second DB read is required)

Roles

Every Nivaro user belongs to exactly one role. Roles are defined in nivaro_roles and are workspace-scoped — the same user can have different effective permissions in different workspaces depending on which role is active.

Manage roles from the Roles page in the admin UI. The left panel lists all roles; selecting a role opens its policies, metadata, and the list of users currently assigned to it.

Role fieldDescription
nameDisplay name shown in the admin UI and user editor
admin_accessWhen true, all permission checks are bypassed
app_accessWhen false, the user cannot log into the admin UI (API-only access)
workspaceThe workspace this role belongs to; null means available in all workspaces

Policies

A policy grants a specific action on a specific collection to the role it belongs to. Policies are stored in nivaro_policies.

Policy fieldDescription
collectionThe table name the policy applies to, e.g. articles
actionOne of: read, create, update, delete
fieldsOptional JSON array of allowed field names. null means all fields are permitted

Policies are additive — if a role has two policies granting read on the same collection with different field lists, the user sees the union of those fields. Add policies from the Roles page by selecting a role and clicking Add Policy.

Admin access

Roles with admin_access: true bypass all policy checks. Admin users can read and write all collections, manage system settings, create other users and roles, and access all admin-only API routes (AI, imports, SLA rules, alert definitions).

The requireAdmin middleware is applied to routes that must only be accessible to admin users. Non-admin users receive a 403 response regardless of their policies.

Deleting a role that still has users assigned to it is blocked at the API level. Reassign or remove those users first before deleting the role.

Field-level access

When a policy includes a fields array, the items API filters response payloads to only include those fields. Fields not in the allowed list are stripped from GET responses, and write attempts to restricted fields are silently ignored.

Field-level access applies to both REST and GraphQL. The getAllowedFields() helper in services/permissions.ts is used by both the items service and GraphQL resolvers to enforce field restrictions consistently.

import { can, getAllowedFields } from '../services/permissions.js';

if (!await can(req.user, 'read', 'articles')) {
  return reply.status(403).send({ error: 'Forbidden' });
}
const fields = await getAllowedFields(req.user, 'read', 'articles');

OIDC flow

Nivaro uses the OpenID Connect Authorization Code flow with PKCE (Proof Key for Code Exchange) via the openid-client library. The identity provider is Microsoft Azure AD.

  1. User navigates to /login in the admin UI and clicks Continue with Microsoft
  2. The admin UI calls GET /api/auth/login
  3. The server generates a PKCE verifier + challenge and a random state, stores them in the session, then redirects to Microsoft's authorization endpoint
  4. After the user authenticates at Microsoft, the browser is redirected to OIDC_REDIRECT_URI with a code and state
  5. The API exchanges the code for tokens, calls findOrCreateFromOIDC() to upsert the user record (syncing first/last name from the ID token), sets req.session.userId, and redirects to ADMIN_URL

The findOrCreateFromOIDC() function matches on external_id (the OIDC sub claim). New users are created with active status and no role — an admin must assign a role before the user has any permissions.

Sessions

Sessions are managed by @fastify/session with Redis as the backing store. Session keys follow the pattern sess:<id>. The session stores only userId — the full user record is loaded from the database on each authenticated request by the authenticate middleware.

COOKIE_SECURE must be false for any HTTP deployment. Setting it to true on an HTTP connection causes the browser to silently discard the session cookie — the OIDC callback appears to succeed but the user is not logged in.

Bearer tokens

The authenticate middleware checks for a Bearer token in the Authorization header before falling back to session-based auth. This enables programmatic API access without browser-based OIDC.

GET /api/items/articles
Authorization: Bearer your-static-token

Bearer tokens are matched against the static_token column in nivaro_users. If a match is found, req.user is set to that user and all subsequent permission checks apply normally.

Static tokens

Static tokens are long-lived credentials suitable for CI pipelines, external integrations, and the @nivaro/sdk. They are stored in plaintext in nivaro_users.static_token — use a sufficiently random value (32+ characters).

Generate and assign a static token from the Users → Edit User page in the admin UI, or via the API:

PATCH /api/users/:id
Authorization: Bearer admin-token
Content-Type: application/json

{ "static_token": "your-new-random-token" }

The @nivaro/sdk accepts a static token at initialization and automatically sends it as a Bearer header on every request:

import { createNivaro } from '@nivaro/sdk';
const nivaro = createNivaro({ url: 'http://localhost:3055', token: 'your-static-token' });

Overview

Workspaces allow multiple logical tenants within the same Nivaro installation, sharing the same database and Redis instance. Each workspace has a unique slug, display name, icon, and color used in the admin UI sidebar switcher.

Workspaces are managed from the Workspaces page in the admin UI (/workspaces). Admins can create, edit, and delete workspaces and assign an icon and accent color. Only admin users can manage workspaces.

The active workspace is tracked in two places:

  • Database — nivaro_users.current_workspace is updated when a user switches workspaces
  • localStorage — the admin UI stores the active workspace ID under the key nivaro_workspace and injects it as an x-workspace header on every API request via an Axios request interceptor

Isolation scope

Workspace isolation applies to collections and roles only. Item data rows in your business tables are not filtered by workspace — full row-level isolation would require a workspace_id FK per business table (a future migration path).

The resolveWorkspace middleware (in middleware/workspace.ts) resolves the active workspace on every request using this priority order:

  1. x-workspace request header (set by the admin UI interceptor)
  2. user.current_workspace from the database
  3. The default workspace UUID (first workspace by creation order)

Collections and roles are filtered with WHERE workspace = ? OR workspace IS NULL — NULL workspace entries are visible in all workspaces.

resolveWorkspace is registered as a preHandler on the collections and roles routes only. Other routes (items, users, etc.) are not workspace-filtered at the API level.

Switching workspaces

The admin UI shows a workspace switcher popover at the bottom of the sidebar. Clicking a workspace calls POST /api/workspaces/:id/switch, which updates nivaro_users.current_workspace, writes the new ID to localStorage, and reloads the page so all queries re-run against the new workspace context.

To switch workspaces programmatically via the API:

POST /api/workspaces/:id/switch
Authorization: Bearer your-token

Or send the x-workspace header directly on any request to target a specific workspace without changing the user's default:

GET /api/collections
Authorization: Bearer your-token
x-workspace: ws-uuid-here

Workflows

Workflows are state machines that can be bound to any collection. Each workflow template defines a set of states and the transitions allowed between them. When a record is started in a workflow, an instance is created that tracks its current state.

Key concepts

ConceptDescription
TemplateThe blueprint — name, description, color, icon. Reusable across collections.
StateA node in the graph. Has a key (machine-readable), label, color. One state is marked initial; one or more can be terminal.
TransitionAn edge from one state to another. Can require specific roles. from_state = null means "from any state."
BindingAttaches a template to a collection. Optional state_field syncs the current state key into a column on the record.
InstancePer-record runtime: current_state, started_at, completed_at.
HistoryImmutable log of every transition taken, including user and optional comment.

WorkflowPanel

On every item edit page, a WorkflowPanel is rendered above the form. If no workflow is bound to that collection, the panel renders nothing. When a workflow is bound:

  • If no instance exists: shows a "Start Workflow" button.
  • If an instance is active: shows the current state badge and available transition buttons (filtered by the user's role).
  • Clicking a transition button opens a confirm + comment form.
  • History is collapsible within the panel.
lock_record on a state prevents editing the record's fields while that state is active — useful for "under review" or terminal states.

Stage Progress Visibility

Each state has a stage_visibility field that controls whether it appears in the stage progress track on the item edit page.

ValueBehaviour
alwaysDefault. State always shown in the stage progress track.
hide_unless_activeHidden unless the record is currently in this state or has visited it.
hideNever shown in the stage progress track.

States & Transitions

States

FieldDescription
keyUnique string identifier used in code (e.g. in_review)
labelDisplay name shown in the admin UI
colorHex color for the state badge
is_initialOne state per template must be marked initial — this is the starting state
is_terminalTerminal states end the workflow. No transitions out are allowed.
lock_recordWhen true, item fields become read-only while in this state
stage_visibilityalways (default) — always shown in stage track. hide_unless_active — hidden unless current or visited. hide — never shown.

Transitions

FieldDescription
from_stateSource state key. null means "from any state"
to_stateDestination state key
labelButton label shown in the WorkflowPanel
required_rolesJSON array of role IDs. Empty = any authenticated user may take this transition
group_labelTransitions with the same group_label are collapsed into a dropdown in the UI

Role gating

Set required_roles on a transition to restrict who can take it. The UI hides buttons the current user is not allowed to use. The API enforces the check server-side.

Admin users bypass all role checks — admin access grants all workflow transitions regardless of required_roles.

Lock on state

When lock_record is true on a state, the item editor disables all fields while the record is in that state. Use this to freeze records under active review or after publishing.

Bindings & Instances

Bindings

A binding links a workflow template to a collection. Once bound, a "Start Workflow" button appears on every item in that collection. Optionally specify a state_field to mirror the current state key into a regular DB column.

Instances

An instance is created when a user clicks "Start Workflow" on an item (or via POST /api/workflows/:id/instance/:collection/:item/start). Each instance tracks a single current_state.

// Start a workflow instance
POST /api/workflows/:templateId/instance/articles/42/start

// Transition to a new state
POST /api/workflows/:templateId/instance/articles/42/transition
{ "to_state": "in_review", "comment": "Ready for review" }

// Get current instance
GET /api/workflows/:templateId/instance/articles/42

History

Every transition is logged to nivaro_workflow_history with the actor, timestamp, from/to states, and optional comment. History is immutable — rows are never updated or deleted.

API reference

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/workflowsList templates
POST/api/workflowsCreate template
GET/api/workflows/:id/statesList states
POST/api/workflows/:id/statesCreate state
POST/api/workflows/:id/transitionsCreate transition
POST/api/workflows/:id/bindingsBind to collection
GET/api/workflows/:id/instance/:col/:itemGet instance + history
POST/api/workflows/:id/instance/:col/:item/startStart instance
POST/api/workflows/:id/instance/:col/:item/transitionTake a transition

Pipeline Engine — Overview

The Pipeline Engine extends the Workflow Engine with a multi-dimensional ownership model. A pipeline template defines states and bindings, and each binding can have an Owner Matrix — a grid of user assignments keyed by dimension filter combinations.

The primary use case is multi-dimensional approval chains: different users own different states depending on attributes of the record (e.g. division, project type, specific project).

ConceptDescription
TemplateThe blueprint — same as a workflow template. States + bindings.
StateSame as workflow states. Supports skip criteria for auto-advancing.
BindingAttaches the template to a collection. Supports state_field sync and auto_start on item create.
DimensionA filter axis on the binding — a field path (e.g. regions.short_name), label, and flags.
Owner GroupA set of users scoped to a state + filter combination. Has a filters JSON array and a priority integer.
Owner MatrixThe UI grid mapping dimension filter values to owner groups per state.

Admin UI

Navigate to Pipelines in the sidebar to manage pipeline templates. Each template has:

  • A states list with skip criteria configuration.
  • A bindings panel for attaching to collections.
  • A dimensions panel for each binding (drag-to-reorder, required flag).
  • An Owner Matrix grid below the binding config.

Dimensions

Dimensions define the filter axes for the Owner Matrix. Each dimension belongs to a binding and references a field path on the bound collection.

FieldDescription
fieldDotted field path, e.g. regions.short_name or project.project_type.name. Supports M2O, M2M, and O2M traversal.
labelDisplay name shown in the matrix filter bar.
is_row_axisExactly one dimension per binding must be the row axis — it becomes the row header in the matrix grid.
sortDisplay order. Drag-to-reorder in the admin UI; persisted via PATCH.
requiredIf true, the user must select a value for this dimension before editing owner assignments.

Field paths

Dimensions support dotted field paths resolved through relation traversal. For example:

  • regions.short_name — M2O: use the short_name field from the related regions record.
  • project.project_type.name — chained M2O: traverse project → project_type → name.
  • divisions.short_name — M2M parent-side: traverse through the junction table to the divisions collection.

Use the field picker in the dimension form to browse and select paths — it handles relation traversal automatically.

Required dimensions must have a value selected before the matrix becomes editable. An amber warning banner appears listing unmet required dimensions.

Owner Matrix

The Owner Matrix is a table where rows are values of the row-axis dimension and columns are workflow states. Each cell holds a set of users — the owners for that combination of row value and state.

Filter bar

Column-filter dimensions appear as searchable comboboxes above the matrix. Selecting a value narrows which owner group is shown per cell. The search is server-side with a 300ms debounce — typing filters items from the full table, not just the initial 100.

Cell states

StateVisualMeaning
EmptyEm dash (—)No owners assigned for this combination.
ExplicitCyan avatar circlesAn owner group exists exactly for this filter context.
InheritedGray faded avatars + "inherited" labelNo exact match — showing owners from a less-specific (base-level) group.
Override indicatorAmber dot on base-level cellThis cell has context-specific overrides defined for optional filter values.

Editing owners

Click any cell to expand it inline. For an explicit cell: add or remove users directly. For an inherited cell: click "Create override for this context" to create a new explicit group scoped to the current filter values, then add users.

Adding rows

Click "+ Add Row" below the matrix. If the row-axis dimension references a related collection, a searchable picker appears. Otherwise, enter a raw value.

Specificity & Priority

When multiple owner groups could apply to a given record, the system uses a specificity-first resolution to pick the most relevant one.

Specificity

Specificity equals the number of filters on an owner group. A group scoped to division=Northeast + project_type=Marketing + project=SpecialProject (3 filters) beats a group scoped to division=Northeast + project_type=Marketing (2 filters) when all three values match the current record.

Priority tie-breaker

When two groups have the same filter count, the priority integer field decides. Lower number = higher priority. Default is 0. Edit priority in the expanded cell panel.

RuleValue
Most filters winsfilter count DESC
Tie-breakpriority ASC (lower = higher priority)
Default priority0

Inherited fallback

If optional filter dimensions are active but no group covers them, the system falls back to the most specific matching group (typically the base-level group with only required filters). The cell shows an "inherited" indicator — the base-level owners are used but no override exists yet.

Create an override by clicking the cell and using "Create override for this context." This creates a new group with the full current filter context, letting you assign different owners for that specific combination.

Conditional Branching

Transitions can carry condition rules so a record's field values decide which paths are offered. In the pipeline template editor, open a transition and use the "Conditions (optional)" section to add field / operator / value rows.

How it behaves

  • A transition is offered on the item page only when ALL of its conditions match the record's current values (AND semantics). No conditions = always offered, subject to required_roles.
  • Branching: create two transitions out of the same state with opposite conditions — e.g. "Approve" when amount lte 10000 and "Escalate" when amount gt 10000. Exactly one is offered per record.
  • Operators: eq, neq, gt, gte, lt, lte, contains, null, nnull. Numeric values are compared numerically; ordering ops fall back to lexicographic comparison for ISO date strings.
  • Server-side revalidation: on execute, the API re-fetches the record and re-evaluates the conditions. If the client's view was stale, the transition is rejected with HTTP 409 "Transition conditions not met".

Storage and API

// Stored as JSON in nivaro_workflow_transitions.condition_rules
// (shared by workflow and pipeline templates):
[
  { "field": "amount", "op": "gt", "value": 10000 },
  { "field": "region", "op": "eq", "value": "EMEA" }
]

// Set via the transitions endpoints — POST/PATCH transition bodies accept
// condition_rules; available-transition listings and the execute endpoint
// both evaluate them.
Null, empty, or malformed condition_rules are treated as "no conditions" — existing transitions behave exactly as before. SDK: the WorkflowTransition type includes condition_rules?: Array<{ field, op, value }> | null.

REST API — Overview & Auth

The Nivaro REST API is a Fastify v5 server running on port 3055. All routes are under the /api prefix. Two authentication mechanisms are supported on every protected endpoint.

Session (browser)

Microsoft OIDC login sets an HttpOnly session cookie. The browser sends it automatically. The admin UI uses withCredentials: true on every request.

EndpointDescription
GET /api/auth/loginStart OIDC login — redirects to Microsoft.
GET /api/auth/callbackOAuth2 callback — exchanges code, sets session cookie.
POST /api/auth/logoutDestroys session and clears cookie.
GET /api/auth/meReturns current user + role. 401 if unauthenticated.

Static token (scripts / SDK)

Pass a static token in the Authorization header. The token is validated against nivaro_users.static_token and the user's role and permissions apply normally.

Authorization: Bearer 3a7f2b9c1d4e...
If an Authorization: Bearer header is present but the token is invalid, the request returns 401 immediately — it does not fall back to the session cookie.

Error responses

All error responses use JSON with an error string field:

{ "error": "Not found" }
{ "error": "Forbidden" }
{ "error": "Invalid token" }

Items API

The generic items API works against any table registered in nivaro_collections. All requests require authentication and pass through the RBAC permission layer.

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/items/:collectionList records. Supports filter, sort, fields, limit, offset, search.
GET/api/items/:collection/:idSingle record by primary key.
POST/api/items/:collectionCreate a record.
PATCH/api/items/:collection/:idUpdate a record (partial).
DELETE/api/items/:collection/:idDelete a record.

Query parameters (GET list)

ParamDefaultDescription
fields* (all allowed)Comma-separated field names: id,name,created_at
filternoneJSON filter object — see Filter DSL below.
sortnoneComma-separated. Prefix - for descending: -created_at,name
limit25Max rows (hard cap 1000).
offset0Row offset for pagination.
page1Shorthand for offset. page=2&limit=25 → offset=25.
searchnoneFulltext search across string/text fields.

Filter DSL

Filters are URL-encoded JSON objects. The key is the field name, the value is an object with an operator and value. Supports scalar operators, logical combinators, and relation traversal.

Scalar operators

// Exact match
?filter={"status":{"_eq":"active"}}

// Greater than
?filter={"amount":{"_gt":1000}}

// Substring / string matching
?filter={"name":{"_contains":"fiber"}}
?filter={"name":{"_ncontains":"draft"}}
?filter={"code":{"_starts_with":"Purchase"}}
?filter={"email":{"_ends_with":"@gmail.com"}}

// Null check
?filter={"deleted_at":{"_null":true}}

// List membership
?filter={"status":{"_in":["active","draft"]}}
OperatorSQL equivalentNotes
_eq= ?Exact equality.
_neq!= ?Not equal.
_gt> ?
_gte>= ?
_lt< ?
_lte<= ?
_inIN (?,...)Value must be a JSON array.
_ninNOT IN (?,...)Value must be a JSON array.
_nullIS NULLValue is ignored (pass true).
_nnullIS NOT NULLValue is ignored (pass true).
_containsLIKE %?%Substring match.
_ncontainsNOT LIKE %?%Substring exclusion.
_starts_withLIKE ?%Prefix match.
_ends_withLIKE %?Suffix match.

Logical combinators

// AND — all conditions must match
?filter={"_and":[{"status":{"_eq":"active"}},{"amount":{"_gt":1000}}]}

// OR — any condition matches
?filter={"_or":[{"status":{"_eq":"active"}},{"status":{"_eq":"pending"}}]}

Relation filters (M2O)

Filter on a related record's fields by using the relation field name (or its alias without _id suffix) as the key and nesting a filter object inside.

// Items whose owner's department is Engineering
?filter={"owner":{"department":{"_eq":"Engineering"}}}

// Nested two levels deep
?filter={"project":{"division":{"name":{"_contains":"fiber"}}}}

Relation filters (O2M / M2M)

Use _some or _none to filter by whether related records exist.

// Items that have at least one tag named "featured"
?filter={"tags":{"_some":{"name":{"_eq":"featured"}}}}

// Items with no rejected approvals
?filter={"approvals":{"_none":{"status":{"_eq":"rejected"}}}}

Static Tokens

Static tokens let scripts, server-side processes, and the SDK authenticate without a browser session. Each user can have one token at a time. Generating a new token immediately invalidates the previous one.

MethodPathAuthDescription
POST/api/users/me/tokenAny authenticated userGenerate a token for yourself.
DELETE/api/users/me/tokenAny authenticated userRevoke your token.
POST/api/users/:id/tokenAdminGenerate a token for another user.
DELETE/api/users/:id/tokenAdminRevoke another user's token.

Response

POST /api/users/me/token
→ 200 { "data": { "token": "3a7f2b9c1d4e5f6a7b8c9d0e1f2a3b4c..." } }

DELETE /api/users/me/token
→ 204 No Content
Tokens are returned only once — on generation. Store them securely. The token value is not readable again after the response is closed; only a hash indicator is stored.

Using a token

# curl
curl -H "Authorization: Bearer 3a7f2b9c..." https://nivaro.example.com/api/items/articles

# fetch
fetch('/api/items/articles', {
  headers: { 'Authorization': 'Bearer 3a7f2b9c...' }
})

Schema & API Docs

Nivaro auto-generates an OpenAPI 3.1 specification from the live nivaro_collections + nivaro_fields metadata. The spec is always current — it is re-built on every request, so adding a new collection shows up immediately without a restart.

EndpointDescription
GET /api/schema.jsonOpenAPI 3.1 spec as JSON. Safe to consume from CI, code generators, Postman, etc.
GET /api/schemaSwagger UI explorer — interactive, try-it-out enabled, Bearer auth persisted.

The spec includes a component schema for every non-hidden collection, a list-response wrapper with data, total, limit, and offset, and full path definitions for GET list, GET by ID, POST, PATCH, and DELETE.

The spec references two security schemes: bearerToken (static token) and sessionCookie. In Swagger UI, click Authorize and paste your static token to make authenticated requests directly from the browser.

Users API

MethodPathAuth required
GET/api/usersAdmin — list all users with pagination.
GET/api/users/:idAny user (own record) or admin.
POST/api/usersAdmin — create a user (email required).
PATCH/api/users/:idOwn record or admin. Admins can change role/status.
DELETE/api/users/:idAdmin — cannot delete yourself.
POST/api/users/me/tokenAny authenticated user — generate own static token.
DELETE/api/users/me/tokenAny authenticated user — revoke own static token.
POST/api/users/:id/tokenAdmin — generate token for another user.
DELETE/api/users/:id/tokenAdmin — revoke another user's token.
POST/api/users/me/delegateAny authenticated user — set own delegation.
Use me as the ID to target the currently-authenticated user. Token endpoints are also covered in the Static Tokens section above.

Delegation fields

Users carry four delegation columns. delegate_id, delegate_expires_at, and is_out_of_office are self-editable (or via POST /api/users/me/delegate); manager_id is admin-only via PATCH /api/users/:id.

FieldTypeNotes
manager_iduuid | nullFK to another user (admin-only).
delegate_iduuid | nullFK to the user who receives ownership while out of office.
delegate_expires_atdatetime | nullWhen delegation lapses; null = indefinite.
is_out_of_officebooleanMaster switch — delegation only applies when true.
 
// Set your own delegation
POST /api/users/me/delegate
{
  "is_out_of_office": true,
  "delegate_id": "8f3c…",
  "delegate_expires_at": "2026-07-01T17:00:00.000Z"
}
The pipeline engine substitutes the delegate for the owner only when is_out_of_office is true, a delegate is set, and the expiry (if any) is in the future.

Delegation & Substitution

Delegation lets a user temporarily hand off their pipeline owner responsibilities to another user. When a user is marked out of office and has an active delegate, the pipeline engine substitutes the delegate wherever the user would otherwise be resolved as an owner.

Setting your own delegation

On your Profile page the Delegation card lets you configure substitution without admin access:

  • Out of office — toggle on to activate delegation. While off, you remain the owner regardless of the delegate setting.
  • Delegate to — pick the user who should receive your ownership. The picker is a searchable combobox of all users.
  • Delegation expires — optional date/time. Leave blank for an indefinite delegation; once the expiry passes, ownership reverts to you automatically.
  • Manager — read-only on your own profile; set by an administrator.
Delegation only takes effect when all three conditions hold: out of office is on, a delegate is selected, and the expiry (if set) is in the future.

Admin management

On the Users → user edit page, administrators see the same Delegation card plus an editable Manager field. Admins can set delegation and the manager relationship for any user.

How substitution works

When the pipeline engine resolves owners for a state, it applies delegation as the final step. Each resolved owner who is out of office with an active, non-expired delegate is replaced by the delegate. The result is de-duplicated, so two owners delegating to the same person collapse to a single entry.

Auto-Start

A binding can be configured to automatically start a pipeline instance whenever a new item is created in the bound collection. Enable auto_start on the binding and optionally set auto_start_state to a specific state ID. If auto_start_state is null, the pipeline starts in the first initial state (ordered by sort). The auto-start is non-blocking — if it fails, the item creation still succeeds.

FieldTypeDescription
auto_startbooleanWhen true, a pipeline instance is created automatically on item create.
auto_start_stateUUID | nullState to start in. Null = first initial state ordered by sort.

DELETE/api/pipelines/owner-group-users/:idRemove a user from a group.

Owner queries (authenticated)

These endpoints resolve actual owners against live record data using the specificity model (filter count DESC, priority ASC). Requires a valid session or static token — not admin-only.

MethodPathDescription
GET/api/pipelines/:id/matrixFull owner matrix for a template: all states → groups → users. No record context — returns configured groups as-is.
GET/api/pipelines/instance/:collection/:item/ownersResolved owners for the record's current pipeline state.
GET/api/pipelines/instance/:collection/:item/owners/allResolved owners for every state in the bound pipeline, keyed by stateId. Single call for full matrix resolution.
GET/api/pipelines/instance/:collection/:item/owners/:stateIdResolved owners for a specific state given the record's filter context (any state, not just the current one).

Owner resolution

Owner groups are matched against the record using the specificity model:

// Specificity algorithm (mirrors the Owner Matrix UI):
// 1. Evaluate each non-default group: all its filters must match the record.
// 2. Sort matched groups by filter count DESC, then priority ASC.
// 3. Winner: the single most specific group. Its users are the resolved owners.
// 4. If no filter-based group matches, fall back to default groups.
// 5. Instance-level manual owners (POST /owners) are merged in last.

// Filter shape — stored on each owner group:
{
  "filters": [
    { "field": "regions.short_name", "op": "eq", "value": "NED", "id_value": 3 },
    { "field": "project.project_type.name", "op": "eq", "value": "CAR", "id_value": 7 }
  ],
  "priority": 0   // lower number = higher priority (tie-breaker only)
}
// id_value: optional FK id used for M2O relation fields (more stable than display text)

Skip criteria

States can be auto-skipped when a record enters them. Skip criteria are evaluated server-side during transitions.

// SkipCriteria shape (stored per state):
{
  "mode": "any",   // "any" = skip if ANY condition true; "all" = skip if ALL true
  "conditions": [
    { "type": "no_owners" },                              // skip if resolved owners = []
    { "type": "field_compare", "field": "amount", "op": "lt", "value": 1000 },
    { "type": "field_empty",    "field": "region" },
    { "type": "field_nonempty", "field": "approved_by" }
  ]
}
